Oh you, most dear sons, I have completed this book which is the latest of medical knowledge along with its completion, and I have finished it through its explanations and declarations. And it has come to my mind that I would complete it for you with this treatise, which is part of the work of hands, namely "surgery".
And since the work of hands is neglected in our region and is despised everywhere, it has been lost and cut off, and nothing remains of it except the small descriptions in books of the ancients that have been written by hand. And from this has come error and vanity, and intentions are closed off, and knowledge is distant.
I think it seems to me that I want to bring to life together the arrangement of this treatise according to the way of exposition and declaration and abbreviation. and I will bring together the forms of cauterizing instruments and other tools for this work with the adjustment of their declaration and preparation as it is necessary.
And because of this reason that no good master surgeons are found in our time, the art of medicine is distant. And it is necessary for him who undertakes it to know anatomy, as Galen says, so long as he knows the joints of the members, and their forms and connections and separations, and has knowledge of bones and nerves and veins and the number of them, and their location and the place of their origin.
And therefore says Hippocrates that a name with a name is much, but with the work is little. and especially in the art of hand.
We tell you at the introduction to this book that whoever is not knowledgeable of the things before mentioned should beware lest they stumble in error and harm people.
in so far as I have wished many times to warn those who take part in this art and abandon their science and sense of experience.
For I have seen a foolish surgeon who cut off the abscess from the scrofulous neck of a woman and cut the arteries of the neck. Why so much blood flows out that the woman fell dead between her hands.
And we have seen another man who treated a stone from an old man, and the stone was large; so he took with him a piece of the bladder, and the man inside died within three days.
And I had already been called to treat him, and I saw the condition of the patient and the great size of the stone, and I knew well that if it was not removed he would die.
And we have seen another surgeon who treated the leg of a duke from our land which was broken, and with the break there was a wound;
and the ignorant surgeon held the break above the wound with stitches by strong thread, and did not leave any linen on the wound at all, and thus left him to his end;
and he commanded that it not be undone.
and thus it remained so that the leg was completely inflamed and the feet came to ruin.
I am summoned to come to him, and I hurry to come to free his leg. and when I loosen it so that it is at peace and he feels no pain.
But all the same the corruption had already taken hold in the member, and I could not heal it;
and the corruption did not cease to spread through the member until the whole limb was completely destroyed.
And I have seen another surgeon who opened up an infected abscess, and then inflamed it through his own ineptitude.
When a chancre is pure of melancholic humour, it does not require iron to be touched if it is in such a place that everything corrupted can be removed from it.
And therefore, very dear son, it is necessary for you to know that the work of hands is divided into two sections: that is to say, work in which there is danger in many conditions;
and I will show you in each place of this book where it has fear and peril.
Why it is necessary for you to guard against it, so that the foolish observer cannot speak badly of you.
If you take up your arms in custody, and undertake your patients lightly and firmly, and employ the best method so that by the grace of God you come to salvation and be praised.
and let the troublesome diseases of bad sanitation;
and put down your arms from those things that make you doubt, and have courage in yourselves so that you can come to the other world of glory.
Galien says in one of his warnings: Do not take on a sick patient who will call you a foolish doctor.
I have written this treatise according to three chapters.
The first chapters are of fire cauteries and of hot medical cauteries, and the chapter is ordered from head to feet.
and of the shapes of instruments, and of iron clamps for cautery, and of all that is necessary in the work.
The second chapter is about cutting and piercing, and of poultices and wounds, and the extraction of arrows, and similar things;
and it deals with the ordering and shapes of instruments.
The third chapter is about restoring dislocations and twists, and similar things;
and it deals with the ordering of instruments from head to foot, and the shapes of instruments.
Therefore, so that we remember the work, it is necessary for me to say the quality of aid and harm in each temperament.
I say that the quality of healing, and the cause of harm, is the longest talk and subtlest science and secret responses;
and many wise people spoke about this, and agreed with it;
and I shorten their words for they are too long because I fear the length.
I say that cauterizing helps universally to every temperament where there is matter, except for two temperaments: it is to know hot constitution with cold matter, and dry constitution with cold matter.
In a hot and dry constitution together with cold matter, they decided one thing and said that cautery is great aid; and the other said the opposite: that cautery is not worth for illness that comes from heat and dryness. For the nature of fire is hot, and it should not be used to cure a hot illness with heat, nor by dryness;
and he who said the opposite says that cautery does great aid for a hot and dry illness that comes in the body of men. Because when you compare the body of man and its moisture to the temperament of fire, you find that the body is cold.
And I agree with this statement. Because I have found it to be true at some point through experience.
And in any way, do not interfere with those who have proved it, and who know by long experience the chapter of cauterizations, and the diversity of constitutions of men, and their dispositions and causes of illnesses, and the cures and the time when.
we have no fear of other constitutions, especially in cold and wet diseases. And all the wise men gathered together and agreed on cauterization.
And know, my son, that combined fire is a secret of cures and of greater goodness than burning medical cauterization.
Because the fire is simple, and it doesn't harm any other member if its name is not known; and it only harms the burned part.
hot remedies come from member to member, causing and bringing grievous sicknesses of difficult recovery to the affected limb. and it may happen that the patient dies.
the fire on account of its greatness and because of the goodness of its substance does not cause harm, if there is no excess.
And I have found this for you through experience and the length of my service and study that I have put into the art, and it was based on a true understanding of things.
and for this reason I excuse the length of my words, because it displeases me to take from you the secret which is resolved by fire and the quality of the work, how it expels diseases from the body, as the philosopher says in demonstrating. Or you receive them in your thoughts.
And know, son, that they agreed on the timing of when cauterizations should be done and selected certain patients.
And I say that cautery is advisable at all times, because the evil growths beneath are put to rights by the aid of cautery. and above all if the cauteries are for urgent pains that cannot wait until a greater evil comes to the member.
And never think this, dear son, as foolish men do; for the disease that is cured by cautery has no relapse. and they say so themselves;
and they say so themselves; but it is not so as they think, for cautery is not but a medicine that moves the complexion and dries the humors which are the cause of pain, and avails more than other medicines in hastening its value and virtue through the efficacy and power of its work.
It is possible that the disease will come upon the patient at some time according to the temperament of the patient and the location of the disease itself.
and the excesses are gathered in him from the acquisition of meats and similar things, unless there are cauterizations administered to the place where he has an excess of superfluity and moisture, such as a burning on the pain, and similar things, and that pain does not return. but this is rare.
And many people do not understand why cauterizations are called the last resort of medicine, and that is true.
but they do not believe that cauterizations are worth after medicine, but their intention is false, and cauterization is the last resort of medicine because when we administer ways of treatment in some illness and they are not effective, then we administer cauterization, and it works.
So now you understand well that cauterization is the last resort of medicine, not as foolish men think.
The ancient ones said that cauters made of golden instrument are more effective than those made of iron, and they did not say this because of the quality of gold but because of its high density.
and they said that the places of cauterization do not become infected, but this is not true for I have tried it and found that it is so in some men.
and golden cauters are worth more than iron ones, just as they said. And anyway when you heat an instrument of gold, you do not know whether it is heated or not by the color of the gold, and it cools down immediately.
and if one heats it too much; they put it in fire; and thus there is enough hindrance.
Now I have written out this chapter from the beginning to the end, so that it will be easier for you to find what you need.
These oil cauterizations are effective against moisture and cold in the head, and there are two types of them: one is done because of a disease called "soda", and another because of many humors that descend from the head to the ears, and for a multitude of headaches, toothaches, and throat pain, as well as all diseases that come from coldness, such as paralysis, epilepsy, apoplexy, and similar maladies.
The form of this cautery is that the patient be purged by a medicinal solution softening the head to three or four parts, according as the virtues and age and habit of the patient can suffer. and then make him recline his head.
And then have him sit with his arms crossed between your hands, and place his hands on the balance scale.
place the root of your palm on the root of his navel between his two eyes; and when it comes to your middle fingers, if it bleeds in the center then heat the cauterizer which is called "olivare", of which this is the shape: And place it on the spot marked with ink, and move your hand downwards and outwards in a twisting motion; then lift your hand straight up, and return to the spot if you see the bone itself clearly small; and if you do not see it, then reheat the cauterizer until you see the bone as I have told you.
after that take a piece of cloth and wet it and make it soft with cotton inside, and place it on the spot, and let it be for three days.
after putting a wet cloth soaked in lard on the spot; and leave it there until the heat is gone. after treating the wound with ointment called "tetrafarmacion", so long as it is healed.
and they said that the older ones, that the longer an open wound stays, the cleaner it becomes. and for this reason does not help much.
And some of them said that the cauterization should be done so thoroughly that part of the bone is burned, and then once what has been burned of the bone is scraped off, it should be cured.
And they say the other that one should let the cautery burn so much on it, and press so hard that you lower to the bone as wide as the strip that women put in their armpits because the humors run out there.
and one should leave the wound open for a long time. after that one should treat and bind it.
And these two ways of cauterizing do not seem to me at all good in every case, except for some men where there is a way of fear.
and it seems to me that I must let it go;
for the joint is weakened by continuous flowing of nature, as we witness in other members;
and similarly when the joint of the patient is weak by nature, and the first sign of cauterizing is more safe and better for me, and from that I work in such a way as to bring about safety.

of toothache (dolor des dens)
When tooth pain comes from cold or hot and the cures of medicine are not worth it, then there is need for a cautery in two ways: and a poultice of butter and a fire cautery.
A poultice of butter is such that you take butter from a cow, and the bottom in a spoon of iron or of tin. Then take cotton and wrap it on the tip of a tent, and soak it in melted butter, and put it on the aching tooth hastily and keep it until it cools down.
and so do it often until the virtue comes to the root of the tooth, and if you see that a woolen and cotton poultice in cold butter, and put on the aching tooth, and put on hot iron until fire comes to the cheekbone of the tooth.
The fire cauterization together is such that you take a dog of iron or tin, and it should be thick so that the fire does not come to the mouth of the patient.
After the heating of the cautery, whose shape will come to be here afterwards, and put it on the tooth and hold your hand until the cautery cools.
do this often, for the pain will be removed that same day or the next at most.
And it is necessary for the patient to fill his mouth with good butter in pressing on that cautery, and then let it drip.
and this is the shape of the cautery:

I say that wounds are diverse according to how they are made, and according to the places where the wounds are made, and of what they are made.
The things by which wounds are made are through a stone falling, and cutting with a sword and knife or lance or club or arrow or similar things;
or those which are made according to the places of the body, such as wounds that strike on the neck, or on the head, or the back, or the belly, or the liver, and similar members;
and I will tell you the treatment of each wound, and I will begin with the simple wounds of the head, because the memory will come in its chapter.
I say that when a simple wound comes to the head, and the bone is not broken, take care if it's from falling of stone or similar things, and the skin is completely torn up and the wound is large, and you slightly doubt of hot abscess: if it is done immediately to stop bleeding from the head itself if blood flows from the wound, and the bleeding occurs on the opposite side of the injured area;

and this is the common method of stitching, and it is that you take one needle or more, according to the quantity of the width of the wound, then leave a space from the head of the wound of about an inch, and insert a needle where there is good thread. and pierce the two heads of the skin with the two heads of the awl which is inside the skin, as far as you make it pierce from that part, and join the two ends of the awl together.

and it does not help to thrust the needles too deep into the flesh and skin, that they cut and open the wound in front of the suturing;

and this manner of stitching with needles is more advisable in small wounds, for it suffices with one needle or two.
The second stitching is common, and it is that you assemble the two pieces of skin and the two pieces of flesh together with one needle in which there is one strong thread in the middle;
and when you have pierced all four pieces together, then remove the needle at the part where you began, in the manner that one sews cloth;
and put a thread of the thickness of a small coin between each stitch;
this stitching is known to men, and I sewed up a wound that a man had on his belly, which was injured by a knife, and the wound was more than one palm long, and it reached as far as two palms into the intestines, and the wound was on the belly.

Now I will tell you the two proper ways of stitching.
take the needle and push it from the outside part up to the inside part;
when it has pierced the core straight through, then turn the tip of the needle or stitch where you had put the needle in, and make it pierce from the inside part up to the outside part.
and the understanding of this stitch is that you sew as tailors do with furs, and leave it once on one side, and take it up again on the other, until the stitching is completely finished.
The second manner of stitching, which the Gauls call properly, is such that some do, who assemble the two parts together naturally, and apply one end of the suture to the other end, in this way:
thread a needle or head of a thread close by, and make it pierce only that place, and let the two ends of the suture remain. then turn the needle, and make it pierce from outside to inside, up to the inner part, with the two ends of the suture.
then make it pierce one and the other from outside to inside, in two other holes of the thread that are on the other side.
and this is the simpler manner of stitching and the most common.
The Gauls call this phrase thus, and some testify to it, that the belly should be sewn with two needles, or thread in each.

of an ulcer or whatever it may be. Know that every wound or abscess, when it festers, is universally called a "fistula"; and indeed when it is filled with pus and flows downward.
A fistula is a hard and white abscess-like thing that forms according to the direction of the node, where one does not feel pain, and it is also hollow like the quill of a bird.

and I have spoken about this in the division of wounds, that every wound that is not healed, and there is no flesh, it's only because of one of the nine causes: that is to say, by the weakness of blood or body; or because of its wickedness; or because it has hard flesh within and on the edges that does not allow new flesh to grow; or there is too much pus; or the wound is rotten and the matter is of bad quality; or the medicine is not good in the treatment; or because the corruption is a manner of plague; or because of the property in that region is slow in digestion and slow in healing, and follows its natural course; where there are veins or bones:
and I have already shown all these causes, and the signs, and the cures of medicine in the division.
Now it is necessary that I inform you about the treatment for fistula made by manual work.
Know that a fistula occurs in every member of the body; for there are fistulas that come to the large veins, and arteries, and nerves, or to the bladder, or to the intestine, or to the bladder, or to any of the ribs, or to the spine of the back, or to any joint of the hands or feet; and thus it can occur in the property of the principal member, and similar lesions.

and if there is any fistula that does not come all the way to the place that I have said, and you have faith in the cure, and you know it well, take a tent of lead or iron, if the fistula is straight, cut into it;
And if the fistula is twisted, then search for it with a thin probe to plunge in, because the probe bends around its twistiness.
and if the fistula has many openings and you cannot well search for it with probes, then purge it through one of the openings, because the moisture runs from one opening to another, and purify.
then seek a puncture to your ability, knowing if there is bone or nerve, and it is sharp in depth, and ask the patient well about the pain he feels when pressing with your hand, and where he feels it.
and when you will truly know the place where it is, and if it is far from a joint, or nerve, or artery, or vein, or in any of the places that I have told you, then cut away according to what I have said, and take out the bad formation and the corrupt flesh that are inside.
and then the cure until it is healed; and if the fistula is well dug from the right place, it is necessary that you go deep as far as you can; then put wet sponges soaked in medicine poultice on it, and keep them tight to the head of the fistula, so that the medicine corrodes the remaining excess at the bottom.

Here begins the book of wounds (or "The Book of Bruises"). This chapter is many times necessary in the art of medicine, and is a remedy for wounds and swellings.
Learned doctor, know that foolish men have fallen from this chapter, which never saw the ancient books, nor read a letter about it.
and because of that reason is estranged the science in our land, for I never found one good;
and I know nothing else, except by the science of ancient books, which I have studied so much that I have treated with science and by experience, and by the habituation of my life.
And I have thus described in this chapter that which is contained, and I have summarized it at the end, and have shown clearly the forms of instruments that are brought to bear, as I have done in these two chapters before.
So then it is fitting that we say the prologue of this book, which are the summaries of words and chapters where the wise man puts his understanding, and remains on the truth, so that those who have been proven wise may know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
I say that whenever a break or dislocation or twisting or crushing comes to anyone, it is necessary that you hasten to heal the patient from one part and then, if nothing else prevents it, as weakness of body, or childbirth, or old age; or if the temperature is too hot, or too cold.
and have him drink cold broths, that is to say, cold joints, and the flesh of hare and goat, and let him not drink wine, nor eat any fatty meats, and do not fill him with meats that fill the veins with blood, until you are in doubt about a hot abscess or an effusion of matter into the limb.

For with such nourishment, the flesh is repaired more quickly and the wound heals sooner.

Of the breaking of the shoulder
